instances</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Your web-app has a runtime that is not supported by the Application Load Balancer</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Your selection is correct</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-filled"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>The route for the health check is misconfigured</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--969">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct options:</p>


<p><strong>The security group of the Amazon EC2 instance does not allow for traffic from the security group of the Application Load Balancer</strong></p>


<p><strong>The route for the health check is misconfigured</strong></p>


<p>An Application Load Balancer periodically sends requests to its registered targets to test their status. These tests are called health checks.</p>


<p>Each load balancer node routes requests only to the healthy targets in the enabled Availability Zones (AZs) for the load balancer. Each load balancer node checks the health of each target, using the health check settings for the target groups with which the target is registered. If a target group contains only unhealthy registered targets, the load balancer nodes route requests across its unhealthy targets.</p>


<p>You must ensure that your load balancer can communicate with registered targets on both the listener port and the health check port. Whenever you add a listener to your load balancer or update the health check port for a target group used by the load balancer to route requests, you must verify that the security groups associated with the load balancer allow traffic on the new port in both directions.</p>


<p>Application Load Balancer Configuration for Security Groups and Health Check Routes:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q26-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q26-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/application/load-balancer-update-security-groups.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/application/load-balancer-update-security-groups.html</a></p>


<p>Incorrect options:</p>


<p><strong>The Amazon Elastic Block Store (Amazon EBS) volumes have been improperly mounted</strong> - You can access the website using the IP address which means there is no issue with the Amazon EBS volumes. So this option is not correct.</p>


<p><strong>Your web-app has a runtime that is not supported by the Application Load Balancer</strong> - There is no connection between a web app runtime and the application load balancer. This option has been added as a distractor.</p>


<p><strong>You need to attach elastic IP address (EIP) to the Amazon EC2 instances</strong> - This option is a distractor as Elastic IPs do not need to be assigned to Amazon EC2 instances while using an Application Load Balancer.</p>


<p>References:</p>


<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/application/load-balancer-update-security-groups.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/application/load-balancer-update-security-groups.html</a></p>


<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/application/target-group-health-checks.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/elasticloadbalancing/latest/application/target-group-health-checks.html</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Secure Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.9759 0.0029 264.54);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.6459 0.1519 154.89);"><use xlink:href="#icon-success"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 28</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.4449 0.0863 157.92);">Correct</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A company wants to store business-critical data on Amazon Elastic Block Store (Amazon EBS) volumes which provide persistent storage independent of Amazon EC2 instances. During a test run, the development team found that on terminating an Amazon EC2 instance, the attached Amazon EBS volume was also lost, which was contrary to their assumptions.</p>


<p>As a solutions architect, could you explain this issue?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>On termination of an Amazon EC2 instance, all the attached Amazon EBS volumes are always terminated</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Your answer is correct</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-success"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>The Amazon EBS volume was configured as the root volume of Amazon EC2 instance. On termination of the instance, the default behavior is to also terminate the attached root volume</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>The Amazon EBS volumes were not backed up on Amazon S3 storage, resulting in the loss of volume</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>The Amazon EBS volumes were not backed up on Amazon EFS file system storage, resulting in the loss of volume</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--971">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>


<p><strong>The Amazon EBS volume was configured as the root volume of Amazon EC2 instance. On termination of the instance, the default behavior is to also terminate the attached root volume</strong></p>


<p>Amazon Elastic Block Store (EBS) is an easy to use, high-performance block storage service designed for use with Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud (EC2) for both throughput and transaction-intensive workloads at any scale.</p>


<p>When you launch an instance, the root device volume contains the image used to boot the instance. You can choose between AMIs backed by Amazon EC2 instance store and AMIs backed by Amazon EBS.</p>


<p>By default, the root volume for an AMI backed by Amazon EBS is deleted when the instance terminates. You can change the default behavior to ensure that the volume persists after the instance terminates. Non-root EBS volumes remain available even after you terminate an instance to which the volumes were attached. Therefore, this option is correct.</p>


<p>Incorrect options:</p>


<p><strong>The Amazon EBS volumes were not backed up on Amazon S3 storage, resulting in the loss of volume</strong></p>


<p><strong>The Amazon EBS volumes were not backed up on Amazon EFS file system storage, resulting in the loss of volume</strong></p>


<p>Amazon EBS volumes do not need to back up the data on Amazon S3 or Amazon EFS filesystem. Both these options are added as distractors.</p>


<p><strong>On termination of an Amazon EC2 instance, all the attached Amazon EBS volumes are always terminated</strong> - As mentioned earlier, non-root Amazon EBS volumes remain available even after you terminate an instance to which the volumes were attached. Hence this option is incorrect.</p>


<p>Reference:</p>


<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/RootDeviceStorage.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/RootDeviceStorage.html</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design High-Performing Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.9759 0.0029 264.54);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.6459 0.1519 154.89);"><use xlink:href="#icon-success"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 29</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.4449 0.0863 157.92);">Correct</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A Big Data processing company has created a distributed data processing framework that performs best if the network performance between the processing machines is high. The application has to be deployed on AWS, and the company is only looking at performance as the key measure.</p>


<p>As a Solutions Architect, which deployment do you recommend?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Spot Instances</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Your answer is correct</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-success"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use a Cluster placement group</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Optimize the Amazon EC2 kernel using EC2 User Data</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use a Spread placement group</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--973">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>


<p>When you launch a new Amazon EC2 instance, the EC2 service attempts to place the instance in such a way that all of your instances are spread out across underlying hardware to minimize correlated failures. You can use placement groups to influence the placement of a group of interdependent instances to meet the needs of your workload. Depending on the type of workload, you can create a placement group using one of the following placement strategies:</p>


<p>Cluster – packs instances close together inside an Availability Zone (AZ). This strategy enables workloads to achieve the low-latency network performance necessary for tightly-coupled node-to-node communication that is typical of HPC applications.</p>


<p>Partition – spreads your instances across logical partitions such that groups of instances in one partition do not share the underlying hardware with groups of instances in different partitions. This strategy is typically used by large distributed and replicated workloads, such as Hadoop, Cassandra, and Kafka.</p>


<p>Spread – strictly places a small group of instances across distinct underlying hardware to reduce correlated failures.</p>


<p>There is no charge for creating a placement group.</p>


<p><strong>Use a Cluster placement group</strong></p>


<p>A cluster placement group is a logical grouping of instances within a single Availability Zone (AZ). A cluster placement group can span peered VPCs in the same Region. Instances in the same cluster placement group enjoy a higher per-flow throughput limit of up to 10 Gbps for TCP/IP traffic and are placed in the same high-bisection bandwidth segment of the network.</p>


<p>Cluster placement groups are recommended for applications that benefit from low network latency, high network throughput, or both. They are also recommended when the majority of the network traffic is between the instances in the group. To provide the lowest latency and the highest packet-per-second network performance for your placement group, choose an instance type that supports enhanced networking.</p>


<p>Image of Cluster placement group:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q20-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q20-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>

<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q20-i3.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q20-i3.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/placement-groups.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/placement-groups.html</a></p>


<p>Incorrect options:</p>


<p><strong>Use Spot Instances</strong> - A Spot Instance is an unused Amazon EC2 instance that is available for less than the On-Demand price. Because Spot Instances enable you to request unused Amazon EC2 instances at steep discounts, you can lower your Amazon EC2 costs significantly. Spot Instances are a cost-effective choice if you can be flexible about when your applications run and if your applications can be interrupted. Since performance is the key criteria, this is not the right choice.</p>


<p><strong>Optimize the Amazon EC2 kernel using EC2 User Data</strong> -  Optimizing the Amazon EC2 kernel won't help with network performance as it's bounded by the EC2 instance type mainly. Therefore, this option is incorrect.</p>


<p><strong>Use a Spread placement group</strong> - A spread placement group is a group of instances that are each placed on distinct racks, with each rack having its own network and power source. The instances are placed across distinct underlying hardware to reduce correlated failures. A spread placement group can span multiple Availability Zones (AZs) in the same Region. You can have a maximum of seven running instances per Availability Zone (AZ) per group.</p>


<p>Reference:</p>


<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/placement-groups.html">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/placement-groups.html</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design High-Performing Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.9759 0.0029 264.54);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.6459 0.1519 154.89);"><use xlink:href="#icon-success"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 30</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.4449 0.0863 157.92);">Correct</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>An IT company has an Access Control Management (ACM) application that uses Amazon RDS for MySQL but is running into performance issues despite using Read Replicas. The company has hired you as a solutions architect to address these performance-related challenges without moving away from the underlying relational database schema. The company has branch offices across the world, and it needs the solution to work on a global scale.</p>


<p>Which of the following will you recommend as the MOST cost-effective and high-performance solution?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon DynamoDB Global Tables to provide fast, local, read and write performance in each region</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Your answer is correct</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-success"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon Aurora Global Database to enable fast local reads with low latency in each region</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Spin up Amazon EC2 instances in each AWS region, install MySQL databases and migrate the existing data into these new databases</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Spin up a Amazon Redshift cluster in each AWS region. Migrate the existing data into Redshift clusters</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--975">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>


<p><strong>Use Amazon Aurora Global Database to enable fast local reads with low latency in each region</strong></p>


<p>Amazon Aurora is a MySQL and PostgreSQL-compatible relational database built for the cloud, that combines the performance and availability of traditional enterprise databases with the simplicity and cost-effectiveness of open source databases. Amazon Aurora features a distributed, fault-tolerant, self-healing storage system that auto-scales up to 64TB per database instance. Aurora is not an in-memory database.</p>


<p>Amazon Aurora Global Database is designed for globally distributed applications, allowing a single Amazon Aurora database to span multiple AWS regions. It replicates your data with no impact on database performance, enables fast local reads with low latency in each region, and provides disaster recovery from region-wide outages. Amazon Aurora Global Database is the correct choice for the given use-case.</p>


<p>Amazon Aurora Global Database Features:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt2-q5-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt2-q5-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/rds/aurora/global-database/">https://aws.amazon.com/rds/aurora/global-database/</a></p>


<p>Incorrect options:</p>


<p><strong>Use Amazon DynamoDB Global Tables to provide fast, local, read and write performance in each region</strong> - Amazon DynamoDB is a key-value and document database that delivers single-digit millisecond performance at any scale. It's a fully managed, multi-region, multi-master, durable database with built-in security, backup and restore, and in-memory caching for internet-scale applications.</p>


<p>Global Tables builds upon DynamoDB’s global footprint to provide you with a fully managed, multi-region, and multi-master database that provides fast, local, read, and write performance for massively scaled, global applications. Global Tables replicates your Amazon DynamoDB tables automatically across your choice of AWS regions. Given that the use-case wants you to continue with the underlying schema of the relational database, DynamoDB is not the right choice as it's a NoSQL database.</p>


<p>Amazon DynamoDB Global Tables Overview:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt2-q5-i2.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt2-q5-i2.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/dynamodb/global-tables/">https://aws.amazon.com/dynamodb/global-tables/</a></p>


<p><strong>Spin up a Amazon Redshift cluster in each AWS region. Migrate the existing data into Redshift clusters</strong> - Amazon Redshift is a fully-managed petabyte-scale cloud-based data warehouse product designed for large scale data set storage and analysis. Amazon Redshift is not suited to be used as a transactional relational database, so this option is not correct.</p>


<p><strong>Spin up Amazon EC2 instances in each AWS region, install MySQL databases and migrate the existing data into these new databases</strong> - Setting up Amazon EC2 instances in multiple regions with manually managed MySQL databases represents a maintenance nightmare and is not the correct choice for this use-case.</p>

The system will also read these log files in parallel on a near real-time basis. The engineering team wants to address any data discrepancies that might arise when the trading system overwrites an existing log file and then tries to read that specific log file.</p>


<p>Which of the following options BEST describes the capabilities of Amazon S3 relevant to this scenario?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>A process replaces an existing object and immediately tries to read it. Until the change is fully propagated, Amazon S3 might return the previous data</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Your answer is correct</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-success"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>A process replaces an existing object and immediately tries to read it. Amazon S3 always returns the latest version of the object</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>A process replaces an existing object and immediately tries to read it. Until the change is fully propagated, Amazon S3 might return the new data</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>A process replaces an existing object and immediately tries to read it. Until the change is fully propagated, Amazon S3 does not return any data</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--977">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>


<p><strong>A process replaces an existing object and immediately tries to read it. Amazon S3 always returns the latest version of the object</strong></p>


<p>Amazon S3 delivers strong read-after-write consistency automatically, without changes to performance or availability, without sacrificing regional isolation for applications, and at no additional cost.</p>


<p>After a successful write of a new object or an overwrite of an existing object, any subsequent read request immediately receives the latest version of the object. Amazon S3 also provides strong consistency for list operations, so after a write, you can immediately perform a listing of the objects in a bucket with any changes reflected.</p>


<p>Strong read-after-write consistency helps when you need to immediately read an object after a write. For example, strong read-after-write consistency when you often read and list immediately after writing objects.</p>


<p>To summarize, all Amazon S3 GET, PUT, and LIST operations, as well as operations that change object tags, ACLs, or metadata, are strongly consistent. What you write is what you will read, and the results of a LIST will be an accurate reflection of what’s in the bucket.</p>


<p>Incorrect options:</p>


<p><strong>A process replaces an existing object and immediately tries to read it. Until the change is fully propagated, Amazon S3 might return the previous data</strong></p>


<p><strong>A process replaces an existing object and immediately tries to read it. Until the change is fully propagated, Amazon S3 does not return any data</strong></p>


<p><strong>A process replaces an existing object and immediately tries to read it. Until the change is fully propagated, Amazon S3 might return the new data</strong></p>


<p>These three options contradict the earlier details provided in the explanation.</p>


<p>References:</p>


<p><a href="https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/Introduction.html#ConsistencyModel">https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AmazonS3/latest/dev/Introduction.html#ConsistencyModel</a></p>

</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Resilient Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.9759 0.0029 264.54);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.6671 0.2202 28.6);"><use xlink:href="#icon-error"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 32</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.5573 0.2161 29.71);">Incorrect</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A media company has created an AWS Direct Connect connection for migrating its flagship application to the AWS Cloud. The on-premises application writes hundreds of video files into a mounted NFS file system daily. Post-migration, the company will host the application on an Amazon EC2 instance with a mounted Amazon Elastic File System (Amazon EFS) file system. Before the migration cutover, the company must build a process that will replicate the newly created on-premises video files to the Amazon EFS file system.</p>


<p>Which of the following represents the MOST operationally efficient way to meet this requirement?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Configure an AWS DataSync agent on the on-premises server that has access to the NFS file system. Transfer data over the AWS Direct Connect connection to an AWS VPC peering endpoint for Amazon EFS by using a private VIF. Set up an AWS DataSync scheduled task to send the video files to the Amazon EFS file system every 24 hours</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Configure an AWS DataSync agent on the on-premises server that has access to the NFS file system. Transfer data over the AWS Direct Connect connection to an AWS PrivateLink interface VPC endpoint for Amazon EFS by using a private VIF. Set up an AWS DataSync scheduled task to send the video files to the Amazon EFS file system every 24 hours</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-incorrect--vFyOv" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8453 0.0845 23.47); color: oklch(0.4224 0.1681 30.2666);">Your answer is incorrect</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-cancel"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Configure an AWS DataSync agent on the on-premises server that has access to the NFS file system. Transfer data over the AWS Direct Connect connection to an Amazon S3 bucket by using a VPC gateway endpoint for Amazon S3. Set up an AWS Lambda function to process event notifications from Amazon S3 and copy the video files from Amazon S3 to the Amazon EFS file system</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Configure an AWS DataSync agent on the on-premises server that has access to the NFS file system. Transfer data over the AWS Direct Connect connection to an Amazon S3 bucket by using public VIF. Set up an AWS Lambda function to process event notifications from Amazon S3 and copy the video files from Amazon S3 to the Amazon EFS file system</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--979">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>


<p><strong>Configure an AWS DataSync agent on the on-premises server that has access to the NFS file system. Transfer data over the AWS Direct Connect connection to an AWS PrivateLink interface VPC endpoint for Amazon EFS by using a private VIF. Set up an AWS DataSync scheduled task to send the video files to the Amazon EFS file system every 24 hours</strong></p>


<p>AWS DataSync is an online data transfer service that simplifies, automates, and accelerates copying large amounts of data between on-premises storage systems and AWS Storage services, as well as between AWS Storage services.</p>


<p>You can use AWS DataSync to migrate data located on-premises, at the edge, or in other clouds to Amazon S3, Amazon EFS, Amazon FSx for Windows File Server, Amazon FSx for Lustre, Amazon FSx for OpenZFS, and Amazon FSx for NetApp ONTAP.</p>


<p>AWS DataSync:
<img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/Digital%20Marketing/House/Editorial/products/DataSync/Product-Page-Diagram_AWS-DataSync_On-Premises-to-AWS%402x.8769b9dea1615c18ee0597b236946cbe0103b2da.png" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/Digital%20Marketing/House/Editorial/products/DataSync/Product-Page-Diagram_AWS-DataSync_On-Premises-to-AWS%402x.8769b9dea1615c18ee0597b236946cbe0103b2da.png" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/datasync/">https://aws.amazon.com/datasync/</a></p>


<p>To establish a private connection between your virtual private cloud (VPC) and the Amazon EFS API, you can create an interface VPC endpoint. You can also access the interface VPC endpoint from on-premises environments or other VPCs using AWS VPN, AWS Direct Connect, or VPC peering.</p>


<p>AWS Direct Connect provides three types of virtual interfaces: public, private, and transit.</p>


<p>AWS Direct Connect VIFs:
<img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt2-q11-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt2-q11-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/premiumsupport/knowledge-center/public-private-interface-dx/">https://aws.amazon.com/premiumsupport/knowledge-center/public-private-interface-dx/</a></p>


<p>For the given use case, you can send data over the Direct Connect connection to an AWS PrivateLink interface VPC endpoint for Amazon EFS by using a private VIF.</p>


<p>Using task scheduling in AWS DataSync, you can periodically execute a transfer task from your source storage system to the destination. You can use the DataSync scheduled task to send the video files to the Amazon EFS file system every 24 hours.</p>


<p>Incorrect options:</p>


<p><strong>Configure an AWS DataSync agent on the on-premises server that has access to the NFS file system. Transfer data over the AWS Direct Connect connection to an AWS VPC peering endpoint for Amazon EFS by using a private VIF. Set up an AWS DataSync scheduled task to send the video files to the Amazon EFS file system every 24 hours</strong> - A VPC peering connection is a networking connection between two VPCs that enables you to route traffic between them privately. You cannot use VPC peering to transfer data over the Direct Connect connection from the on-premises systems to AWS. So this option is incorrect.</p>


<p><strong>Configure an AWS DataSync agent on the on-premises server that has access to the NFS file system. Transfer data over the AWS Direct Connect connection to an Amazon S3 bucket by using public VIF. Set up an AWS Lambda function to process event notifications from Amazon S3 and copy the video files from Amazon S3 to the Amazon EFS file system</strong> - You can use a public virtual interface to connect to AWS resources that are reachable by a public IP address such as an Amazon Simple Storage Service (Amazon S3) bucket or AWS public endpoints. Although it is theoretically possible to set up this solution, however, it is not the most operationally efficient solution, since it involves sending data via AWS DataSync to Amazon S3 and then in turn using an AWS Lambda function to finally send data to Amazon EFS.</p>


<p><strong>Configure an AWS DataSync agent on the on-premises server that has access to the NFS file system. Transfer data over the AWS Direct Connect connection to an Amazon S3 bucket by using a VPC gateway endpoint for Amazon S3. Set up an AWS Lambda function to process event notifications from Amazon S3 and copy the video files from Amazon S3 to the Amazon EFS file system</strong> - You can access Amazon S3 from your VPC using gateway VPC endpoints. You cannot use the Amazon S3 gateway endpoint to transfer data over the AWS Direct Connect connection from the on-premises systems to Amazon S3. So this option is incorrect.</p>

</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design High-Performing Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.9759 0.0029 264.54);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.6671 0.2202 28.6);"><use xlink:href="#icon-error"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 33</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.5573 0.2161 29.71);">Incorrect</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A leading social media analytics company is contemplating moving its dockerized application stack into AWS Cloud. The company is not sure about the pricing for using Amazon Elastic Container Service (Amazon ECS) with the EC2 launch type compared to the Amazon Elastic Container Service (Amazon ECS) with the Fargate launch type.</p>


<p>Which of the following is correct regarding the pricing for these two services?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are charged based on Amazon EC2 instances and Amazon EBS Elastic Volumes used</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-incorrect--vFyOv" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8453 0.0845 23.47); color: oklch(0.4224 0.1681 30.2666);">Your answer is incorrect</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-cancel"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are charged based on vCPU and memory resources that the containerized application requests</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are just charged based on Elastic Container Service used per hour</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct answer</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type is charged based on EC2 instances and EBS volumes used. Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type is charged based on vCPU and memory resources that the containerized application requests</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--981">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>


<p><strong>Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type is charged based on EC2 instances and EBS volumes used. Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type is charged based on vCPU and memory resources that the containerized application requests</strong></p>


<p>Amazon Elastic Container Service (Amazon ECS) is a fully managed container orchestration service. ECS allows you to easily run, scale, and secure Docker container applications on AWS.</p>


<p>Amazon ECS Overview:
<img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/diagrams/product-page-diagrams/product-page-diagram_ECS_1.86ebd8c223ec8b55aa1903c423fbe4e672f3daf7.png" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://d1.awsstatic.com/diagrams/product-page-diagrams/product-page-diagram_ECS_1.86ebd8c223ec8b55aa1903c423fbe4e672f3daf7.png" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/ecs/">https://aws.amazon.com/ecs/</a></p>


<p>With the Fargate launch type, you pay for the amount of vCPU and memory resources that your containerized application requests. vCPU and memory resources are calculated from the time your container images are pulled until the Amazon ECS Task terminates, rounded up to the nearest second.
With the EC2 launch type, there is no additional charge for the EC2 launch type. You pay for AWS resources (e.g. EC2 instances or EBS volumes) you create to store and run your application.</p>


<p>Incorrect options:</p>


<p><strong>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are charged based on vCPU and memory resources that the containerized application requests</strong></p>


<p><strong>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are charged based on Amazon EC2 instances and Amazon EBS Elastic Volumes used</strong></p>


<p>As mentioned above - with the Fargate launch type, you pay for the amount of vCPU and memory resources. With EC2 launch type, you pay for AWS resources (e.g. EC2 instances or EBS volumes). Hence both these options are incorrect.</p>


<p><strong>Both Amazon ECS with EC2 launch type and Amazon ECS with Fargate launch type are just charged based on Elastic Container Service used per hour</strong></p>


<p>This is a made-up option and has been added as a distractor.</p>


<p>References:</p>


<p><a href="https://aws.amazon.com/ecs/pricing/">https://aws.amazon.com/ecs/pricing/</a></p>
</div></div><div data-purpose="domain-pane" class="domain-pane--domain-pane--Pw9dK"><div class="domain-pane--domain-pane-header--2263m ud-heading-md">Domain</div><div class="ud-text-md">Design Cost-Optimized Architectures</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-wrapper--2bGiz"><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane--sIcOh result-pane--accordion-panel--TEJg7"><div class="result-pane--question-header-wrapper--3DCpC"><div class="result-pane--question-header--pTUOx"><span class="result-pane--question-header-collapsed-text--WVdEr"><span class="result-pane--pane-title--f-2kd ud-heading-md"><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon" class="result-pane--answer-status-icon--ebl6C"><span class="result-pane--question-icon-background--AskFJ" data-purpose="question-result-header-status-icon-background" style="background: oklch(0.9759 0.0029 264.54);"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium" style="color: oklch(0.6459 0.1519 154.89);"><use xlink:href="#icon-success"></use></svg></span></span><span>Question 34</span><span data-purpose="question-result-header-status-label" style="color: oklch(0.4449 0.0863 157.92);">Correct</span></span><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-large ud-btn-ghost ud-btn-text-md ud-btn-icon ud-btn-icon-large"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-medium ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-collapse"></use></svg></button></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="result-pane--question-format--PBvdY ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="question-prompt"><p>A retail company uses AWS Cloud to manage its technology infrastructure. The company has deployed its consumer-focused web application on Amazon EC2-based web servers and uses Amazon RDS PostgreSQL database as the data store. The PostgreSQL database is set up in a private subnet that allows inbound traffic from selected Amazon EC2 instances. The database also uses AWS Key Management Service (AWS KMS) for encrypting data at rest.</p>


<p>Which of the following steps would you recommend to facilitate end-to-end security for the data-in-transit while accessing the database?</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Create a new security group that blocks SSH from the selected Amazon EC2 instances into the database</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Create a new network access control list (network ACL) that blocks SSH from the entire Amazon EC2 subnet into the database</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-radio-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use IAM authentication to access the database instead of the database user's access credentials</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Your answer is correct</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-success"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Configure Amazon RDS to use SSL for data in transit</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--983">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct option:</p>


<p><strong>Configure Amazon RDS to use SSL for data in transit</strong></p>


<p>You can use Secure Socket Layer / Transport Layer Security (SSL/TLS) connections to encrypt data in transit. Amazon RDS creates an SSL certificate and installs the certificate on the DB instance when the instance is provisioned. For MySQL, you launch the MySQL client using the --ssl_ca parameter to reference the public key to encrypt connections. Using SSL, you can encrypt a PostgreSQL connection between your applications and your PostgreSQL DB instances. You can also force all connections to your PostgreSQL DB instance to use SSL.</p>


<p><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q31-i1.jpg" style="display: none;"><span class="ud-component--base-components--open-full-size-image"><div class="open-full-size-image--wrapper--R4gIm" data-purpose="open-full-size-image"><img src="https://assets-pt.media.datacumulus.com/aws-saa-pt/assets/pt3-q31-i1.jpg" alt="" loading="eager"><button type="button" class="ud-btn ud-btn-medium ud-btn-link ud-btn-text-sm open-full-size-image--backdrop--Zor3j"><svg aria-label="Larger image" role="img" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-large ud-icon-color-neutral"><use xlink:href="#icon-search"></use></svg></button></div></span>
via - <a href="https://aws.amazon.com/rds/features/security/">https://aws.amazon.com/rds/features/security/</a></p>


<p>Incorrect options:</p>


<p><strong>Use IAM authentication to access the database instead of the database user's access credentials</strong> - You can authenticate to your database instance using AWS Identity and Access Management (IAM) database authentication. IAM database authentication works with MySQL and PostgreSQL. With this authentication method, you don't need to use a password when you connect to a database instance. Instead, you use an authentication token.</p>


<p>IAM authentication is just another way to authenticate the user's credentials while accessing the database. It would not significantly enhance the security in a way that enabling SSL does by facilitating the in-transit encryption for the database.</p>


<p><strong>Create a new security group that blocks SSH from the selected Amazon EC2 instances into the database</strong></p>


<p><strong>Create a new network access control list (network ACL) that blocks SSH from the entire Amazon EC2 subnet into the database</strong></p>


<p>Both these options are added as distractors. You cannot SSH into an Amazon RDS database instance.</p>

The news network has recently expanded into new geographies in Europe and Asia. The technical teams at the overseas branch offices have reported huge delays in uploading large video files to the destination Amazon S3 bucket.</p>


<p>Which of the following are the MOST cost-effective options to improve the file upload speed into Amazon S3 (Select two)</p></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-result-pane-expanded-content--Og5Vc"><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Correct selection</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use Amazon S3 Transfer Acceleration (Amazon S3TA) to enable faster file uploads into the destination S3 bucket</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-correct--PLOEU" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8101 0.0873 162.22); color: oklch(0.3072 0.0555 158.67);">Your selection is correct</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-filled"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use multipart uploads for faster file uploads into the destination Amazon S3 bucket</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Create multiple AWS Direct Connect connections between the AWS Cloud and branch offices in Europe and Asia. Use the direct connect connections for faster file uploads into Amazon S3</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-skipped--1NDPn" data-purpose="answer"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.6722 0.0355 279.77);"><use xlink:href="#icon-checkbox-empty"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Use AWS Global Accelerator for faster file uploads into the destination Amazon S3 bucket</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--answer-result-pane--Niazi"><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-incorrect--vFyOv" data-purpose="answer"><div><span data-purpose="answer-result-header-user-label" class="result-pane--answer-by-user-label--PSH86 ud-heading-xs" style="background: oklch(0.8453 0.0845 23.47); color: oklch(0.4224 0.1681 30.2666);">Your selection is incorrect</span></div><div class="answer-result-pane--answer-body--cDGY6" data-purpose="answer-body"><span data-purpose="answer-result-body-selection-icon" class="answer-result-pane--answer-selection-icon--O6Xkn"><svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" class="ud-icon ud-icon-small" style="color: oklch(0.2565 0.0265 278.04);"><use xlink:href="#icon-wrong-selection"></use></svg></span><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-heading-md rt-scaffolding" id="answer-text"><p>Create multiple AWS Site-to-Site VPN connections between the AWS Cloud and branch offices in Europe and Asia. Use these VPN connections for faster file uploads into Amazon S3</p></div></div></div></div><div class="result-pane--question-related-fields--c3m--"><div class="overall-explanation-pane--overall-explanation--G-hLQ ud-form-group"><label class="ud-heading-md ud-form-label ud-heading-sm" for="form-group--985">Overall explanation</label><div data-purpose="safely-set-inner-html:rich-text-viewer:html" class="ud-text-md rt-scaffolding" id="overall-explanation"><p>Correct options:</p>


<p><strong>Use Amazon S3 Transfer Acceleration (Amazon S3TA) to enable faster file uploads into the destination S3 bucket</strong></p>


<p>Amazon S3 Transfer Acceleration enables fast, easy, and secure transfers of files over long distances between your client and an S3 bucket. Amazon S3TA takes advantage of Amazon CloudFront’s globally distributed edge locations. As the data arrives at an edge location, data is routed to Amazon S3 over an optimized network path.</p>


<p><strong>Use multipart uploads for faster file uploads into the destination Amazon S3 bucket</strong></p>


<p>Multipart upload allows you to upload a single object as a set of parts. Each part is a contiguous portion of the object's data. You can upload these object parts independently and in any order. If transmission of any part fails, you can retransmit that part without affecting other parts. After all parts of your object are uploaded, Amazon S3 assembles these parts and creates the object. In general, when your object size reaches 100 MB, you should consider using multipart uploads instead of uploading the object in a single operation. Multipart upload provides improved throughput, therefore it facilitates faster file uploads.</p>


<p>Incorrect options:</p>


<p><strong>Create multiple AWS Direct Connect connections between the AWS Cloud and branch offices in Europe and Asia. Use the direct connect connections for faster file uploads into Amazon S3</strong> - AWS Direct Connect is a cloud service solution that makes it easy to establish a dedicated network connection from your premises to AWS. AWS Direct Connect lets you establish a dedicated network connection between your network and one of the AWS Direct Connect locations.
Direct connect takes significant time (several months) to be provisioned and is an overkill for the given use-case.</p>


<p><strong>Create multiple AWS Site-to-Site VPN connections between the AWS Cloud and branch offices in Europe and Asia. Use these VPN connections for faster file uploads into Amazon S3</strong> - AWS Site-to-Site VPN enables you to securely connect your on-premises network or branch office site to your Amazon Virtual Private Cloud (Amazon VPC). You can securely extend your data center or branch office network to the cloud with an AWS Site-to-Site VPN connection. A VPC VPN Connection utilizes IPSec to establish encrypted network connectivity between your intranet and Amazon VPC over the Internet.
VPN Connections are a good solution if you have low to modest bandwidth requirements and can tolerate the inherent variability in Internet-based connectivity. Site-to-site VPN will not help in accelerating the file transfer speeds into S3 for the given use-case.</p>


<p><strong>Use AWS Global Accelerator for faster file uploads into the destination Amazon S3 bucket</strong> - AWS Global Accelerator is a service that improves the availability and performance of your applications with local or global users. It provides static IP addresses that act as a fixed entry point to your application endpoints in a single or multiple AWS Regions, such as your Application Load Balancers, Network Load Balancers or Amazon EC2 instances. AWS Global Accelerator will not help in accelerating the file transfer speeds into S3 for the given use-case.</p>


<p>References:</p>
